  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_28c1eb31-bd39-4a75-bad2-c5fcae694e12'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer6365643363407079487">Marina Nemat's peaceful childhood in Tehran was shattered when the Iranian Revolution of 1979 ushered in a new era of Islamic rule. After complaining to her teachers about lessons being replaced by Koran study, Marina was arrested late one evening. She was taken to the notorious prison, Evin, where she was interrogated and tortured. Aged sixteen, she was sentenced to death</span>
  <span id="freeText6365643363407079487" style="display:none">Marina Nemat's peaceful childhood in Tehran was shattered when the Iranian Revolution of 1979 ushered in a new era of Islamic rule. After complaining to her teachers about lessons being replaced by Koran study, Marina was arrested late one evening. She was taken to the notorious prison, Evin, where she was interrogated and tortured. Aged sixteen, she was sentenced to death. <br /><br /><i>Prisoner of Tehran</i> is the astonishing account of one woman's remarkable courage in the face of terror and her quest for freedom.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The book is under copy right laws, so a PDF version is not available. As for the book itself, you can buy it in English on amazon.ca, amazon.com, and <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The book is under copy right laws, so a PDF version is not available. As for the book itself, you can buy it in English on amazon.ca, amazon.com, and amazon.co.uk. As for translations, please try your local bookstores. The French is available on amazon.fr, and the German on amazon.de.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_244411934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/244411934" />
    <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma"><img alt="Nandakishore Varma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583648733p2/6237864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/244411934?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nandakishore Varma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nandakishore Varma" href="/user/show/6237864-nandakishore-varma">Nandakishore Varma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 5551628507" href="/book/show/16422671-prisoner-of-tehran">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer244411934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14978825675047449097">A 16-year-old girl, swept off the streets and put in prison for the most token resistance against a totalitarian regime... saved from execution at the eleventh hour by her jailor, who had fallen in love with her... forced to marry him, to save herself, and to live as his "trophy wife"... escaping from the claustrophobic marriage when her husband is killed by hired goons of the regime... finally managing to escape to Canada, the "free and democratic" West, with her lover...<br/><br/>It could be the script </span>
  <span id="freeText14978825675047449097" style="display:none">A 16-year-old girl, swept off the streets and put in prison for the most token resistance against a totalitarian regime... saved from execution at the eleventh hour by her jailor, who had fallen in love with her... forced to marry him, to save herself, and to live as his "trophy wife"... escaping from the claustrophobic marriage when her husband is killed by hired goons of the regime... finally managing to escape to Canada, the "free and democratic" West, with her lover...<br /><br />It could be the script of a Bollywood movie.<br /><br />Which is why this book came down to two stars for me.<br /><br />I have no doubt Marina is factual in the account of her travails. I have no illusions about the Islamic Republic of Iran, or the Evin prison. I am sure that if the regime of the Shah was totalitarian, the theocratic one that replaced it is even more so. <br /><br />No, it was the tone of the writing: the self-righteousness. It is as though the author, being a Russian immigrant, is never somehow fully Iranian and is viewing Iranians through a foreign lens. Also, many a time I found her peddling her "Christian forbearance" in the face of authoritarian Islam (to be fair, I am sure that this is not done purposefully - Marina's strong religious belief seems to have indeed helped her get through a terrible period); this also put me off. The book seemed to be written for a Western audience eager to believe the worst about Iran. Like I said, it is like a movie script, the heroes and villains clearly defined: good winning against evil in the end, and everybody living happily ever after.<br /><br />I am happy for Marina that her personal story ended happily. I mourn for the hundreds of others who are prisoners of totalitarian regimes, whose stories have no such happy ending and are therefore unheard of. But the book itself, I found unimpressive. Maybe a more nuanced writing would have helped.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14978825675047449097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1047197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1047197" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54752-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184819140p2/54752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1047197?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/54752-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1047197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7324829116471923338">This is the most moving, powerful and astonishing book I've read since "The End of the Spear."<br/>In a matter-of-fact tone that makes her vivid descriptions all the more compelling, Marina Nemat describes how she became a political prisoner in the early days of Iran's Islamic Revolutionary government for the crime of asking her calculus teacher to teach calculus instead of government propaganda. She was spared execution for this horrendous crime (but not imprisonment) only through the intercession o</span>
  <span id="freeText7324829116471923338" style="display:none">This is the most moving, powerful and astonishing book I've read since "The End of the Spear."<br />In a matter-of-fact tone that makes her vivid descriptions all the more compelling, Marina Nemat describes how she became a political prisoner in the early days of Iran's Islamic Revolutionary government for the crime of asking her calculus teacher to teach calculus instead of government propaganda. She was spared execution for this horrendous crime (but not imprisonment) only through the intercession of a powerful interrogator who had a crush on her, and later force her to marry him.<br />As I read these chapters, I marveled that anyone could endure such unspeakable cruelties and remain sane. Then I was stopped short by the realization: She was just 16 when this ordeal began.<br />If you're getting scared away because all this sounds terribly depressing, trust me, it's not (taken as a whole). It's inspiring.<br />The chapters in which she flashes back to her earlier childhood in Iran are as captivating as the prison chapters, and in some ways almost as heartbreaking.<br />It's no wonder that it took two decades before the author was able to talk about and write about these experiences. That she survived to do it, that she was courageous enough to do it, and that she writes it with such remarkable clarity is a work of grace for the rest of us.<br />"Prisoner of Tehran" is the book of the year for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7324829116471923338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16595705056403152560">An absorbing read that I finished in 24 hours.<br/>The real life memoirs of Marina Nemat, whose troubles with the despotic and murderous Islamist regime in Iran begins when she walks out of calculus class in protest at the replacement of the subject of calculus with Islamic and political propaganda, and is joined by 3o other girls.a<br/>Soon afterwards she is arrested by Islamic Republican guards and taken to the notorious Evin prison in Tehran where she is beaten, tortured and sentenced to death.<br/>A real w</span>
  <span id="freeText16595705056403152560" style="display:none">An absorbing read that I finished in 24 hours.<br />The real life memoirs of Marina Nemat, whose troubles with the despotic and murderous Islamist regime in Iran begins when she walks out of calculus class in protest at the replacement of the subject of calculus with Islamic and political propaganda, and is joined by 3o other girls.a<br />Soon afterwards she is arrested by Islamic Republican guards and taken to the notorious Evin prison in Tehran where she is beaten, tortured and sentenced to death.<br />A real window into the horrors of the Islamic Republic of Iran under the diabolical Ayatollah Khomeini At Even she sees many of her friends tortured to death or executed.<br />Her life is spared by a prison guard who has fallen in love with her and intercedes to commute her death sentence, but at a a price, she must convert to Islam and marry him.<br />He too is eventually assassinated by the Islamic Regime.<br />The book alternates chapter by chapter between the horrors of Evin prison and Marina's childhood in Tehran, and how Iran is turned into a hellish tyranny by the Islamic Revolution of 1979.<br />A must read both as a book on life and on a regime whose horrors (especially against girls and women) who's horrors have been completely ignored by the world and who get a free pass from leftwing 'human rights' activists because of its anti-Western credentials.<br />Comment Comment | Permalink</span>
  <a data-text-id="16595705056403152560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Asking her calculus teacher to teach calculus rather than talking about political issues.   <span id="freeText2218804435865268409" style="display:none">This book was amazing, I highly recommend it to everyone! It is about an Iranian girl that was taken political prisoner (at the age of 16) in Iran during the early 1980's. Her crime? Asking her calculus teacher to teach calculus rather than talking about political issues. The teacher refused and told Marina to leave class if she didn't like it, she left and so did the rest of the class. Even though the subject matter is heavy, the book is written in a very readable way. I read this book yesterday, couldn't put it down. Make sure you have some tissues handy!</span>

<div id="review_100576431" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100576431" />
    <a title="Valarie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3023326-valarie"><img alt="Valarie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327883044p2/3023326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100576431?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valarie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valarie" href="/user/show/3023326-valarie">Valarie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3023326-valarie?shelf=biography-memoir">biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3023326-valarie?shelf=middle-east">middle-east</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3023326-valarie?shelf=in-translation">in-translation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100576431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14393626756144571019">This was a very interesting book, with a beautiful and inspiring story. The writing itself was bland and often contrived, but I can forgive that because the author is writing in her third or fourth language. However, the story was almost too perfect. The villain finds redemption right before he dies, the heroine is reunited with her prince charming, and everybody lives happily ever after. It is difficult to believe that, in circumstances where so many others died, Nemat openly flouted the govern</span>
  <span id="freeText14393626756144571019" style="display:none">This was a very interesting book, with a beautiful and inspiring story. The writing itself was bland and often contrived, but I can forgive that because the author is writing in her third or fourth language. However, the story was almost too perfect. The villain finds redemption right before he dies, the heroine is reunited with her prince charming, and everybody lives happily ever after. It is difficult to believe that, in circumstances where so many others died, Nemat openly flouted the government's authority and still managed to escape after serving only two years in a relatively comfortable prison (when you compare to other dictatorships, that is). I don't mean to doubt this brave woman, because to imply that she fabricated the story would be awful, but the characters just seemed too angelic and heroic to be believable. Perhaps she reimagined her experiences to make them more understandable, or to disguise the atrocities committed against fellow humans. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14393626756144571019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2297313" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2297313" />
    <a title="Pantea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/127606-pantea"><img alt="Pantea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1182613987p2/127606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2297313?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pantea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pantea" href="/user/show/127606-pantea">Pantea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2297313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9953420782112424343">One of the better books I've read in a long time. Always so interesting for me to read about other people's experience during the Iran Revolution. I was too young to remember much but it definitely had a major impact on my life and those of my family/family friends, etc. This woman's experience was so moving. So hard to believe she experienced all that she did and at such a young age - she was only 16 when they arrested her. I had read other reviews of this book that criticized her memory of exa</span>
  <span id="freeText9953420782112424343" style="display:none">One of the better books I've read in a long time. Always so interesting for me to read about other people's experience during the Iran Revolution. I was too young to remember much but it definitely had a major impact on my life and those of my family/family friends, etc. This woman's experience was so moving. So hard to believe she experienced all that she did and at such a young age - she was only 16 when they arrested her. I had read other reviews of this book that criticized her memory of exact details, etc. I think it's important to keep in mind that these are her memoirs and remembering the past is not always crystal clear in terms of specific dates, places, events. For a first time writer, I think she did a great job... I really liked the book and found it hard to put down. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9953420782112424343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9624051868329910733"><b>3.5/5</b><br/><br/>Gripping, extraordinary biography.📝<br/><br/>In 1982, <b>Marina Nemat</b> a Christian girl from Tehran was only 16 years old when she was arrested on false charges by the notorious Revolutionary guards of Ayotallah Khomeini. She was tortured and put up in the infamous <i>Evin</i> prison while she saw her friends getting executed.<br/>But she got a chance to live!<br/>Her interrogator <b>Ali</b> fell in love with her and got her out. In return, she had to convert to Islam and marry him!<br/>Although she is not happy about her marriage t</span>
  <span id="freeText9624051868329910733" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5</b><br /><br />Gripping, extraordinary biography.📝<br /><br />In 1982, <b>Marina Nemat</b> a Christian girl from Tehran was only 16 years old when she was arrested on false charges by the notorious Revolutionary guards of Ayotallah Khomeini. She was tortured and put up in the infamous <i>Evin</i> prison while she saw her friends getting executed.<br />But she got a chance to live!<br />Her interrogator <b>Ali</b> fell in love with her and got her out. In return, she had to convert to Islam and marry him!<br />Although she is not happy about her marriage to him, she learns to love his family. Towards the end of the book, <b>Ali</b> is assassinated by his friends and coworkers, and his dying wish is for his father to take Marina back.<br />The book jumps back and forth between <b>Nemat</b>'s time as a prisoner – both in Evin and in her marriage – and earlier, carefree days when she fell in puppy love with a young Muslim working to overthrow the Shah.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer274715291324595169">I loved this book, couldn't put it down! "Prisoner of Tehran" is a moving memoir about a Christian girl in Iran during the Islamic revolution. She is arrested for 'anti-government' activities (such heinous crimes as walking out of her calculus class because the teacher would only talk about politics, not calculus). She is sentenced to death but is saved by a prison guard who then forces her to convert to Islam and marry him. The book describes her stay in prison and her forced marriage while als</span>
  <span id="freeText274715291324595169" style="display:none">I loved this book, couldn't put it down! "Prisoner of Tehran" is a moving memoir about a Christian girl in Iran during the Islamic revolution. She is arrested for 'anti-government' activities (such heinous crimes as walking out of her calculus class because the teacher would only talk about politics, not calculus). She is sentenced to death but is saved by a prison guard who then forces her to convert to Islam and marry him. The book describes her stay in prison and her forced marriage while also flashing back to her childhood in Iran and the onset of the revolution. <br />I have a great deal of respect and admiration for the courage that it must have taken Nemat not only to live through this ordeal but also to tell her story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="274715291324595169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1368476303" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1368476303" />
    <a title="Lucy Qhuay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7115693-lucy-qhuay"><img alt="Lucy Qhuay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564407818p2/7115693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1368476303?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Qhuay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Qhuay" href="/user/show/7115693-lucy-qhuay">Lucy Qhuay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=autobiography-biography-memoir">autobiography-biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=ultimate-favourites">ultimate-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=my-poor-heart">my-poor-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=politics">politics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=oh-my-the-horror">oh-my-the-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7115693-lucy-qhuay?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368476303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13084424458330516994"><br/>'Prisoner of Tehran' reads as if it was a romance, but it is not. It is a heart-pounding, heartbreaking true story of a young Iranian girl facing the brutal horrors of the Islamic Revolution.<br/><br/>In January 1982, 16-year-old Marina Nemat was arrested and sent to Evin, Tehran's most famous (and feared) prison, for daring to protest against the current political regime and the way schools seemed more intent on political propaganda rather than teaching kids proper subjects such as Math and History.<br/><br/>Brand</span>
  <span id="freeText13084424458330516994" style="display:none"><br />'Prisoner of Tehran' reads as if it was a romance, but it is not. It is a heart-pounding, heartbreaking true story of a young Iranian girl facing the brutal horrors of the Islamic Revolution.<br /><br />In January 1982, 16-year-old Marina Nemat was arrested and sent to Evin, Tehran's most famous (and feared) prison, for daring to protest against the current political regime and the way schools seemed more intent on political propaganda rather than teaching kids proper subjects such as Math and History.<br /><br />Branded an enemy of God and the nation, she was tortured and sentenced to death, only to narrowly escape at the last moment, due to the help of one of her jailers, Ali, who was able to use his family's influences to reduce her sentence to life in prison.<br /><br />However, Ali's gesture would have a price: if Marina didn't convert to Islam and marry him, he would find a way to arrest her family and the young man she loved, Andre, and have them all executed.<br /><br />What choice did she have? Sick and tired of all the senseless deaths she witnessed at Evin and faced with the possibility of being the one responsible for the deaths of her loved ones, she agreed to leave behind her Christian faith and every principle that had been a part of her life thus far and be Ali's wife.<br /><br />Marina spent the next two years as a prisoner of the state, but above all, as a prisoner of Ali, a man who held the lives of everyone she loved in his hands, a man who seemed to desperately love her, but that she couldn't love no matter how hard she tried.<br /><br />I must say that, from every single shocking and heartbreaking thing that happened to her, her time with Ali was the most difficult thing for me to process. <br /><br />It all started with me being creeped out, due to his support of a rotten system that killed thousands, then hating him for forcing things that should happen naturally and be joyfully given.<br /><br />Somewhere along the way, Marina and I saw he wasn't a soulless beast. He was a very sad man, who tried to do what he thought best, misguided as he was. <br /><br />He actually tried to break free from the system and fought against it. It's sad that he met a tragic fate just when he was finally doing something good and trying to change his life. <br /><br />I'm still trying to comprehend the ambiguity of feelings Ali provoked in me, but who knows if I'll ever get over it?<br /><br />I won't say much more about her journey, because I truly think everybody should read this book and actually live the experience as I did. <br /><br />I felt that I was by Marina's side throughout the entire ordeal. Sometimes I was Marina, saw things through her eyes and felt the whole spectrum of emotion, from her faith and hope, to her horror, fear and anguish.<br /><br />In truth, this was one of those life-changing books that appear unannounced in our lives from time to time and I can't be grateful enough for that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13084424458330516994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer50980663" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1789812287835161159">I had not heard of this book before I added it on my list of books to read by Iranian authors and the only reason I wanted to read it was that I had read an autiobiography of anybody that was a political prisoner of the Islamic Republic and particularly, had spent time in Evin prison. <br/>Evin prison was built by the Shah and during his reign, when I was a child is when I was introduced to the word prison and though my parents never talked about the torture and horrible things that went on behind it</span>
  <span id="freeText1789812287835161159" style="display:none">I had not heard of this book before I added it on my list of books to read by Iranian authors and the only reason I wanted to read it was that I had read an autiobiography of anybody that was a political prisoner of the Islamic Republic and particularly, had spent time in Evin prison. <br />Evin prison was built by the Shah and during his reign, when I was a child is when I was introduced to the word prison and though my parents never talked about the torture and horrible things that went on behind its walls, whenever Evin prison was mentioned, it seemed to always be in hushed voices because it was too horrible of a place to talk to about where all kinds of evil acts were committed.....Well, after reading this book, I am even more fearful of Evin Prison. <br /><br />The author was a bit older than me when the Islamic Revolution took place (most of story written in a voice of a 13 yr old) but unlike me, she was not sheltered from what was going on around her. She was an only child of Russian descendant, Christian parents that really did not talk to her much about anything and she came and went freely and they had no idea she was getting involved in politics in a time where if you were on what was deemed the wrong side (against the Revolution), you would be jailed, tortured and/or killed. <br /><br />The author got involved in demonstrations against the new Islamic State and spent a little over 2 yrs behind Evin where she was horribly tortured and was (stop reading if you plan on reading the book since I am going to give a lot away) blindfolded, put in front of a firing squad to die and granted clemency just seconds before the firing squad starting firing by a man named Ali who was an interrogator who had seen her, unbeknownst to her, fallen in love with her and had miraculously gotten her a pardon from Ayatollah Khomeini (the architect of the Revolution) himself. She then is forced into marrying Ali and forging a new life with him. You learn about the friendship she makes with other female prisoners, about how violent and scary the times were in Iran and in some ways continue to be. <br /><br />This woman's experience is extremely tragic and she suffered so much so young but she was extremely lucky to live to tell the tale. She had never aspired to be a writer but what compelled her to finally talk about her experience (she never talked about what she went through) is when a Canadian journalist was captured in Iran, brutally tortured, raped and finally killed and she felt like she had been silent for long enough and in the comfort of her new life in Canada, she wanted to speak out for the political prisoners of Iran and from all other countries and tell their story.<br /><br />The only reason I give this only two stars is that Marina would leave any reader totally terrified of all things Iranian. She does not attempt, in even one sentence, to say that though the currnet Iranian government might have some shady practices, the Iranian people are good adn the country is good and beautiful and we have this incredibly deep and rich history etc. She is clear on what her goal is which is to educate people on the plight of political prisoners but in doing so, she will definitely put off any person in ever visiting Iran. <br /><br />Maybe my interpretation of this book is a bit skewed and I will admit that since I indeed am an Iranian/American who grew up in Iran during the Shah's regime and lived through the Islamic Revolution but I have dealt with so much ignorance in my years in American regarding Americans and the way they view Iranians and their culture and particularly about Iranian politics, it just seems that a book that focuses purely on the evils of the Islamic Republic, just feeds into all the negative ideas the Western world already has about Iran.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1789812287835161159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_177905389" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177905389" />
    <a title="Canadian Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2103966-canadian-reader"><img alt="Canadian Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580905464p2/2103966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177905389?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Canadian Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Canadian Reader" href="/user/show/2103966-canadian-reader">Canadian Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2103966-canadian-reader?shelf=prisons-and-prisoners">prisons-and-prisoners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2103966-canadian-reader?shelf=persia-iran">persia-iran</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2103966-canadian-reader?shelf=autobiography-and-memoir">autobiography-and-memoir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177905389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15192094945196641286">After the 1979 Islamic Revolution, Marina Nemat was arrested at the age of sixteen. She spent more than two years in Tehran’s infamous Evin Prison for political prisoners. There she was tortured and came very close to execution.<br/><br/>Her memoir is certainly a compelling one, but it lacks stylistic merit, provides little insight into the emotional experiences of political prisoners, and raises many questions. The author’s reconstruction of dialogue is weak and wooden. Interviews with Ms. Nemat are more</span>
  <span id="freeText15192094945196641286" style="display:none">After the 1979 Islamic Revolution, Marina Nemat was arrested at the age of sixteen. She spent more than two years in Tehran’s infamous Evin Prison for political prisoners. There she was tortured and came very close to execution.<br /><br />Her memoir is certainly a compelling one, but it lacks stylistic merit, provides little insight into the emotional experiences of political prisoners, and raises many questions. The author’s reconstruction of dialogue is weak and wooden. Interviews with Ms. Nemat are more revealing and rewarding than her book.<br /><br />I understand that there is some controversy over the the incidents recounted in the memoir. Did they actually occur as reported? I'd be curious to read narratives by others who survived Evin to compare. Certainly some aspects of Ms. Nemat's experience seem to match details reported by the news media: the lack of a trial and the use of bastinado (foot whipping). However, as a western reader, I had trouble believing that a prison interrogator (even one with Ali's apparent status) would have had the power to marry an inmate, never mind take her in and out of the facility, including on holiday to the Caspian Sea. <br /><br />As baffling as the interrogator’s marriage to Nemat (a Christian) was his parents’ ready acceptance of her as a daughter. The marriage might have made more sense if aspects of Iranian culture (including attitudes towards converting to Islam and prisoner "rehabilitation") had been discussed. Ms. Nemat says she told her interrogator-husband's sister the threats that Ali had made to force her into marriage. Although his sister was shocked, there appears to have been little reaction beyond this. Surely there would have been a ripple effect through the family. <br /><br />The book’s strongest sections concern Ms. Nemat’s early experiences at school, her family holidays by the Caspian Sea, and the recollection of her love for a young man who later died in a political demonstration. Nemat's Russian grandmother's story is also fascinating. The author writes that her mother destroyed Nemat’s grandmother's handwritten memoir. <br /><br />The memoirist's strained relationship with her parents was also puzzling. What was it about her parents that made them unwilling to discuss their daughter’s two years in captivity once she’d been freed? <br /><br />The entire book would have been improved by the inclusion of information about the place of religious minorities in Iran (Christians, Zoroastrians, Jews, and Baha'i's) prior to the Islamic Revolution. The reader needs context. <br /><br />In the end, I found myself wondering how the memoir might have read if the author had first recorded her memories in Farsi and then had had them translated by a professional translator. Would that have made the book deeper and more emotionally resonant?</span>
  <a data-text-id="15192094945196641286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117036517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117036517" />
    <a title="Carrie Elizabeth Rundhaug" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3804537-carrie-elizabeth-rundhaug"><img alt="Carrie Elizabeth Rundhaug" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275271675p2/3804537.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117036517?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie Elizabeth Rundhaug" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie Elizabeth Rundhaug" href="/user/show/3804537-carrie-elizabeth-rundhaug">Carrie Elizabeth Rundhaug</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117036517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17701564689571855777">In the Amsterdam airport I headed into one of the many bookstores to look at magazines however I didn’t have much time so I was kind of rushing thru the store however while I was walking by a table with English books on it I noticed this book right away. I picked it up and read the back cover and was instantly drawn to this book. Knowing I would have plenty of time to read it between the flights and my layovers. Once I got to my gate and was able to sit down I instantly started reading it. The b</span>
  <span id="freeText17701564689571855777" style="display:none">In the Amsterdam airport I headed into one of the many bookstores to look at magazines however I didn’t have much time so I was kind of rushing thru the store however while I was walking by a table with English books on it I noticed this book right away. I picked it up and read the back cover and was instantly drawn to this book. Knowing I would have plenty of time to read it between the flights and my layovers. Once I got to my gate and was able to sit down I instantly started reading it. The book captured my attention right away and it was hard to put it down.<br /><br />Heart wrenching, captivating, exhilarating, tragic, and beautiful is a few that come to mind. Marina Nemat invites you into her past, with all those words meshing together to make every scene that she describes. Her emotions start pouring out, like an open diary, more and more so as you flip every page. But first, she begins to tell you of the day, the 16 year old her, got arrested and put into Evin Prison for simply having friends that stood up for what they believed in, that was against what others believed in.<br /><br />She is eventually forced into marriage by one of the guards who have fallen in love with her. Although she is not happy about her marriage to Ali she learns to love his family. Towards the end of the book Ali, Marina’s Muslim husband, is assassinated by those he called friends and coworkers. His dying wish is that is father takes Marina back to her family. <br /><br />This work was not the first writing that was published by Marina but it was the first book. At her high school Marina published several articles that discussed her views on the government. However, what is different with this book is that she tells her story in an engrossing and eloquent manner. I could not put this book done. <br /><br />Marina does a great justice to every character is the book by showing that reality is not as simple as black and white. She shows the humanity and kindness of the guard who forced her to marry him.<br /><br />Reading the memoirs of Marina Nemat has made me appreciate where I was born and raised. Sometimes we all take for granted what we have and it takes a reality check to bring us back to normalcy. <br />One quote we all need to remember is the following: “Ali, do you see what violence does to people? You kill them, and they kill you. When is it going to end, only after everybody is dead?”<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17701564689571855777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText1678687706609263645" style="display:none">Again, read many years ago but never forgotten. <br /><br />The events described in the book is hard to digest, incredibly moving and devastating. It's so tragic how a 16 year old girl was dragged from her normal life to a prison full of nightmares for not believing in what the rest of the people around believed in.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_94941255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94941255" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13779-k"><img alt="K" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94941255?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/13779-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K by: </span>
      La Petite Américaine
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=memoirs">memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=mideastwomen">mideastwomen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=inspiring-story-uninspired-book">inspiring-story-uninspired-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=intense-sad-dark-or-bleak">intense-sad-dark-or-bleak</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13779-k?shelf=thank-god-i-wasn-t-born-there">thank-god-i-wasn-t-born-there</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94941255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12281624667050747823">"Prisoner of Tehran" is a gripping story, and one of the unusual memoirs that actually deserves to be published and read -- if we can believe the story, that is. <br/><br/>Marina Nehmat writes about her childhood growing up in Iran, and her arrest and imprisonment for anti-government activities (sadly minor by our standards) in the infamous Evin prison. Her life up until that point seemed pretty believable, and comparable to other memoirs I've read about Iranian life once the Ayatollah took over. The stor</span>
  <span id="freeText12281624667050747823" style="display:none">"Prisoner of Tehran" is a gripping story, and one of the unusual memoirs that actually deserves to be published and read -- if we can believe the story, that is. <br /><br />Marina Nehmat writes about her childhood growing up in Iran, and her arrest and imprisonment for anti-government activities (sadly minor by our standards) in the infamous Evin prison. Her life up until that point seemed pretty believable, and comparable to other memoirs I've read about Iranian life once the Ayatollah took over. The story became a bit fantastic, though, when she wrote about a prison guard falling in love with her, rescuing her from a firing squad minutes before her scheduled execution, and forcing her to marry him and receive his protection. I guess James Frey stole my innocence, because I just had to go to good old Wikipedia at that point to see whether I should be believing this.<br /><br />And sure enough, Wikipedia came through. Apparently Monireh Baradaran, a fellow Evin inmate, wrote a letter together with some other former Evin inmates protesting the publication of "Prisoner of Tehran" (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.utoronto.ca/prisonmemoirs/Protest.pdf">http://www.utoronto.ca/prisonmemoirs/...</a>) stating among other things that the execution scene was impossible and that Marina's descriptions of prison life did not match the reality. In an amazon review of "Prisoner of Tehran" (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RKVRYKYNY2AX9/ref=cm_cr_pr_viewpnt#RKVRYKYNY2AX9">http://www.amazon.com/review/RKVRYKYN...</a>), Monireh challenges the book on a variety of levels. Although I thought that some of her arguments seemed a bit personal and petty (she claims that Marina inflates her prescience and precociousness as a child, which is arguably true of most memoirists and plays a very trivial role in the book), her other contentions appear more factual and difficult to dispute (why would the Ayatollah permit Marina's release when sons of his close friends and relatives went unpardoned?).<br /><br />On the other hand, other former inmates of Evin and other Iranian prisons have written letters in support of Marina and her book (these sites, unfortunately for me, were in Farsi). So I guess we'll never know. Monireh accuses Marina of having an agenda, but she appears to have one of her own and we'll never know who's right.<br /><br />Three stars, then. The story is gripping, if you can believe it. I found the writing is so-so, but certainly forgivable for a memoir. In any case, it was a quick read that held my interest and a memoir that wasn't all about some privileged person's narcissistic whining but actually had something to say. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12281624667050747823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23873169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23873169" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/439937-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328297665p2/439937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23873169?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/439937-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/439937-jim?shelf=biography-memoir">biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/439937-jim?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/439937-jim?shelf=middle-east">middle-east</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23873169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6046488884605604507">I've been on somewhat of a tour of repression of political dissent recently, having read accounts of horrible treatment of individuals in El Salvador, Cambodia, Thailand, and a few other places. Therefore it is no surprise I picked up this memoir of a woman's stay in Iran's notorious Evin prison. It is almost unimaginable what humans can do to each other and how they find excuses for the pain they inflict, how easy it is for some to be swept up almost unquestioningly to do the dirty work of evil</span>
  <span id="freeText6046488884605604507" style="display:none">I've been on somewhat of a tour of repression of political dissent recently, having read accounts of horrible treatment of individuals in El Salvador, Cambodia, Thailand, and a few other places. Therefore it is no surprise I picked up this memoir of a woman's stay in Iran's notorious Evin prison. It is almost unimaginable what humans can do to each other and how they find excuses for the pain they inflict, how easy it is for some to be swept up almost unquestioningly to do the dirty work of evil people (even if those devils have rationalized to themselves otherwise). It is particularly disheartening when the atrocities are carried out by those who profess to be doing it for religious reasons, though everyone knows it is about power. No doubt hundreds of thousands of innocents have been collateral damage at the hands of cruel jailers and death squads, around the world over our collective history. And although I hate when Americans cross the line in treatment of prisoners, and we have on occasion, I still think I would much rather be held by us that just about anywhere else on the globe. In this case the victims were primarily the former comrades of elements that helped overthrow the Shah, and who then became targets for the fundamentalists who brooked no criticism from the left, and especially from women. In this remembrance, Nemat is saved from execution by a smitten interrogator and will be forced to renounce her faith (Christianity, as her grandmothers were Russian Orthodox) and even marry her oppressor in order to escape certain death or continued incarceration. For me, who has many Iranian friends, it is hard to imagine this mistreatment, though clearly it has been a hallmark of the mullah-controlled nation. The story is chilling and delves into more than just her stint at Evin, but she avoids making it into an evangelical tome. How much is fudged, a common fear nowadays with nonfiction, I don't know, but my sense is that she is pretty straight and honest about her story, without much embellishment. Luckily for her she made it to Canada, had a family, and became one important voice for the lost and against such horrors. I will also add that I am amazed and humbled by people who, even knowing their actions can have dire results, stand up against blatant evils.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6046488884605604507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1905291922" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1905291922" />
    <a title="Rose Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23492259-rose-scott"><img alt="Rose Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430782815p2/23492259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1905291922?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose Scott" href="/user/show/23492259-rose-scott">Rose Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1905291922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14425655731454174733">In late 1970’s Iran, the Shah’s government was on shaky ground and the relative peace of Marina Nemat’s childhood erupted into unrest and restrictions on freedom, culminating in the death of her friend. As a young woman and a Christian minority, she dared to participate in protests against the Ayatollah Khomeini and spoke out at her school when the political climate affected her education. <br/>In 1982, at the age of sixteen, she was arrested, along with several of her friends and taken to Evin priso</span>
  <span id="freeText14425655731454174733" style="display:none">In late 1970’s Iran, the Shah’s government was on shaky ground and the relative peace of Marina Nemat’s childhood erupted into unrest and restrictions on freedom, culminating in the death of her friend. As a young woman and a Christian minority, she dared to participate in protests against the Ayatollah Khomeini and spoke out at her school when the political climate affected her education. <br />In 1982, at the age of sixteen, she was arrested, along with several of her friends and taken to Evin prison where she was interrogated and tortured. She was slated for execution, but at the last minute, a prison guard intervened and her sentence was commuted to mere “life imprisonment.” Little did Nemat realize the price she would have to pay for being allowed to live. <br />After several months of suffering and watching her friends be sent to their deaths, she is forced to make the most difficult choices of her life. Eventually freedom comes, but at a cost. Her traumatic experiences prove almost impossible to express to others and she recognizes that she has changed. It is a prison of another kind. <br />	The story is a poignant and emotional journey. Though some have criticized the book for being “movie like” or patently untrue, notwithstanding the slight variations in memory that may exist over time, this memoir has the ring of truth. The author should only be commended for her courage to write such a raw and painful story.				<br />She comes to discern that her captors, even the Ayatollah himself, are, like all of us, a complex mixture of good and bad. This understanding of human nature and its shades of gray is impressive, when it is so much easier to paint people as either morally upright or evil. What’s more, though she fully grasps the wrongs done to her, she made the decision to forgive—of this she states, “I knew forgiveness didn’t come at once and complete, beautifully packaged and tied with a red ribbon, but it came little by little. And my forgiving…wasn’t going to erase the pain...but would help me rise above the past and face all that had happened…so I could be free” (p.236). 	<br />After many years of silence, Nemat chose to heal by giving voice to her trials and becoming a witness to the egregious errors of political imprisonment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14425655731454174733" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1494702225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494702225" />
    <a title="Judith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8338351-judith"><img alt="Judith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332462634p2/8338351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1494702225?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judith" href="/user/show/8338351-judith">Judith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143052173" href="/book/show/2713485-prisoner-of-tehran">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1494702225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4575141956278892991">I registered a book at BookCrossing.com!<br/><a href='http://www.BookCrossing.com/journal/12549014' rel='nofollow noopener'>http://www.BookCrossing.com/journal/12549014</a><br/><br/>I find memoirs by people from other countries interesting, as a rule. I especially like it when I can read two or three books about the same approximate time period from different perspectives, as it gives me a more rounded feeling for the country and the time. So this book interested me. I had read Reading Lolita in Tehran, which took place not long after the main events in this story. Both illuminate what Iran </span>
  <span id="freeText4575141956278892991" style="display:none">I registered a book at BookCrossing.com!<br /><a href="http://www.BookCrossing.com/journal/12549014" rel="nofollow noopener">http://www.BookCrossing.com/journal/12549014</a><br /><br />I find memoirs by people from other countries interesting, as a rule. I especially like it when I can read two or three books about the same approximate time period from different perspectives, as it gives me a more rounded feeling for the country and the time. So this book interested me. I had read Reading Lolita in Tehran, which took place not long after the main events in this story. Both illuminate what Iran was like in the early days of the Islamic Republic of Iran (the country is still Islamic). <br /><br /> Marina Nemat was arrested at age 16 for activities against the state. She was in high school at the time, opposed to the new Islamic state and vocal about her objections. She was in the infamous Evin prison in Tehran for over two years. <br /><br /> Her story reads like a novel. Early on, she is rescued from the firing squad seconds before she would have been dead. Later, her rescuer, an interrogator at the prison, wants her to marry him, threatening harm to her family if she does not. He is assassinated, but lives long enough to ask his family to bring Marina back to her family.<br /><br /> I am not the only one who is skeptical about the details of this story. Several persons who were in Evin Prison around the same time have even written letters to the book publisher, saying she is not telling the whole story and is making some things up. For example, they say that anyone who would be permitted to marry an interrogator would have to be an informant. And they say the rescue from execution is simply not believable. <br /><br /> I would love to hear corroboration from some of the persons who were there, most particularly the family of the interrogator she married. Other prisoners who were in the same rooms with her might also be able to confirm some facts. I have not found this kind of information online, but I'm not saying it isn't there. <br /><br /> I found it a highly readable book with a lot of details about the regime and the prison. Worth reading, but with some skepticism. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4575141956278892991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1818095654" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1818095654" />
    <a title="Nitika Nayar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61783824-nitika-nayar"><img alt="Nitika Nayar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480665263p2/61783824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1818095654?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nitika Nayar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nitika Nayar" href="/user/show/61783824-nitika-nayar">Nitika Nayar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1818095654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer773421050923824973">This book puts forth an account of Iran during the reign of Ayotallah Khomeini and the experience of lay citizens under the rule in a very matter-of-fact manner. The use of simplistic language did not fail to create an emotional stir in the my mind, as I read over the atrocities carried out against the prisoners. <br/><br/>I must admit I had sympathy, if not an attraction towards Ali. Regardless of him working with the Khomeini administration, I felt there was a good guy underneath. A dark guardian angel,</span>
  <span id="freeText773421050923824973" style="display:none">This book puts forth an account of Iran during the reign of Ayotallah Khomeini and the experience of lay citizens under the rule in a very matter-of-fact manner. The use of simplistic language did not fail to create an emotional stir in the my mind, as I read over the atrocities carried out against the prisoners. <br /><br />I must admit I had sympathy, if not an attraction towards Ali. Regardless of him working with the Khomeini administration, I felt there was a good guy underneath. A dark guardian angel, if you will. Being under a conservative, repressive regime can only but taint your beliefs and values, however I believe Ali was quite liberal when it came to this. He was alright with Marina practising her own religion privately, despite being a devout Muslim. He was alright with her meeting Andre, her previous lover, one last time before embarking upon her new life. His family showered more love over Marina than her own parents could ever shell out. Over and above everything, even in his dying moment, he called out to his father to see to it that she'd reunite with her parents. It was no surprise when I poured out over his death. None of her other male interests had that kind of impression on me. Andre was too plain to have an opinion on. There was something mystical about Arash, however I didn't get to quite embrace that, as he unfortunately lived a very short life. <br /><br />This is a must read for anyone who's interested in knowing more about Iran, before and after the Khomeini dictatorship, the torturous practises taking place behind the notorious Evin prison walls, the Middle East in general or for anyone really who doesn't have anything to do for 2-3 hours. A fast yet must read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="773421050923824973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1539518867" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1855265288474555001">As far as the events go, I don't think anyone can even begin to fathom what it's like to be a political prisoner in an Iranian prison .. And to be arrested at 16 makes it ten times worst .. <br/><br/>But I think that we can all learn and relate to marina wanting to believe in the good people have within them .. Believing that not everyone is purely evil and we all have the ability to be kind .. <br/><br/><br/>Her hope and strength throughout these horrible events are inspiring .. Sacrificing herself and agreeing to marr</span>
  <span id="freeText1855265288474555001" style="display:none">As far as the events go, I don't think anyone can even begin to fathom what it's like to be a political prisoner in an Iranian prison .. And to be arrested at 16 makes it ten times worst .. <br /><br />But I think that we can all learn and relate to marina wanting to believe in the good people have within them .. Believing that not everyone is purely evil and we all have the ability to be kind .. <br /><br /><br />Her hope and strength throughout these horrible events are inspiring .. Sacrificing herself and agreeing to marry Ali to spare her family and Andre is admirable .. <br /><br />But I found myself sympathizing with Ali despite hating him in the beginning .. Even after he raped marina .. By the time his life was over I realized he's just like any other middle eastern / Muslim husband .. He believes it's his right to force himself on his wife and demand sex even if she refuses and objects .. <br />I truly believe he loved her and wanted to protect her .. By the end I believed that he never intended to follow through with his threats to harm Andre or marina's family .. It was just a manipulative method to protect the person he loved .. <br />He didn't know how else to love marina other than to protect her even if it wasn't the best method .. <br /><br /><br />And I think that in the end Marina's mixed feelings about Ali was the hardest thing she struggled with .. Specially after his death .. <br /><br /><br />I cried like a baby .. <br /><br />It was a great book .. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1855265288474555001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8436866926497431964">2.5 star!<br/><br/>I know this is her memories and so naturally I should not have any reason to doubt the sequence of events.   <span id="freeText8436866926497431964" style="display:none">2.5 star!<br /><br />I know this is her memories and so naturally I should not have any reason to doubt the sequence of events. But I found it a bit inconvincible! <br /><br />The beginning of the book was promising when talking about how Jung people were the main Protestants who formed rallies against the Islamic revolution. Even when she first arrived the prison, it was interesting to read and know what was happening in women prisons and how they were treated or more precisely tortured.<br /><br /> But the moment Ali entered the story line, the story turned out to a movie!<br /><br />You know the end but you don’t know how it will happen – kind of suspense!<br />That particular part of her life with Ali, which was more than half , was boring and his death was the part that ruined the whole novel!<br /></span>

<div id="review_766719355" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/766719355" />
    <a title="Mahsa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17370032-mahsa"><img alt="Mahsa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428884242p2/17370032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/766719355?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mahsa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mahsa" href="/user/show/17370032-mahsa">Mahsa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer766719355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6753831489826547059">Nemat's memoirs is an easy read. The most fascinating aspect for me was author's devotion to portrait true sides of each character and go beyond the limits of black and white side in judging her opponents. She doesn't tell her story with hatred but a heart filled with forgiveness and healing! Despite of the brutal tortures and pressures, she has made peace with her self and moved on with a great hope for the future. <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aT7qCgh5fMVngvDcp6A9fn4lwyk+afSTJ8aae4g8OYkDodxuDQkYWALAEYf07WlB3podDjS1nwb5Tlf7Z3inXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EykcF4zYQjFp39odnNMtnqkYPN7gaIaQ5Ou0cF3yfyR5tipziagmrAydO0bPnnmhCafi+eq07QU6Y3nwsrbh8A==')})
  }
//]]>

Rather than returning Soraya\'s dowry, as custom required before taking a second wife, he plotted with four friends and a counterfeit mullah to dispose of her. Together, they accused Soraya of adultery. Her only crime was cooking for a friend\'s widowed husband. Exhausted by a lifetime of abuse and hardship, Soraya said nothing, and the makeshift tribunal took her silence as a confession of guilt. They sentenced her to death by stoning: a punishment prohibited by Islam but widely practiced. Day by day sometimes minute by minute Sahebjam deftly recounts these horrendous events, tracing Soraya\'s life with searing immediacy, from her arranged marriage and the births of her nine children to her husband\'s increasing cruelty and her horrifying execution, where, by tradition, her father, husband, and sons hurled the first stones.  This is one woman\'s story, but it stands for the stories of thousands of women who suffered and continue to suffer the same fate.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/163705.Marina_Nemat">About Marina Nemat</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/163705.Marina_Nemat"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1301337336p3/163705.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/163705.Marina_Nemat">Marina Nemat

<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3990396837582416395">Marina Nemat was born in 1965 in Tehran, Iran. After the Islamic Revolution of 1979, she was arrested at the age of sixteen and spent more than two years in Evin, a political prison in Tehran, where she was tortured and came very close to execution. She came to Canada in 1991 and has called it home ever since. Her memoir of her life in Iran, Prisoner of Tehran, was published in Canada by Penguin C</span>
  <span id="freeText3990396837582416395" style="display:none">Marina Nemat was born in 1965 in Tehran, Iran. After the Islamic Revolution of 1979, she was arrested at the age of sixteen and spent more than two years in Evin, a political prison in Tehran, where she was tortured and came very close to execution. She came to Canada in 1991 and has called it home ever since. Her memoir of her life in Iran, Prisoner of Tehran, was published in Canada by Penguin Canada in April 2007, has been published in 28 other countries, and has been an international bestseller. MacLean’s Magazine has called it “…one of the finest (memoirs) ever written by a Canadian.” Prisoner of Tehran has been short listed for many literary awards, including the Young Minds Award in the UK and the Borders Original Voices Award in the US. On December 15, 2007, Marina received the inaugural Human Dignity Award from the European Parliament, and in October 2008, she received the prestigious Grinzane Prize in Italy. In 2008/2009, she was an Aurea Fellow at University of Toronto’s Massey College, where she wrote her second book, After Tehran: A Life Reclaimed, which was published by Penguin Canada on September 18, 2010, and has so far been published in four countries.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3990396837582416395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
